## Glossary
The glossary clarifies how key terms are used in the context of the e-GRM design. Where terms have multiple interpretations in other domains, the definitions below should be treated as the system-specific meaning.
| Term | Definition |
| Acknowledgement | Confirmation that a grievance has been received and registered, and (where possible) communication to the complainant about next steps and timelines. |
| Administration console | Administrative interface used to configure and govern the e-GRM (e.g., users, roles, departments, queues, templates, SLA plans, notification rules). |
| Agent | A staff user (case handler) who manages grievances in the agent console (e.g., reviewing, updating status, assigning, responding). |
| Agent console | Operational interface used by case handlers, team leads, and managers to search, view, process, and track grievances and related tasks. |
| Alerts and notices | System notifications triggered by events (e.g., new grievances, messages, overdue conditions) to support timely handling and oversight. |
| Anonymous complaint | A grievance submitted without identifying information about the complainant; still recorded and managed with appropriate follow-up where feasible. |
| Appeal | A request by a complainant for review of a grievance decision/outcome through the defined escalation/appeals pathway. |
| Assisted intake | Registration of a grievance in the e-GRM by an officer on behalf of a complainant who used an offline channel (e.g., in-person, phone call, letter, complaint box). |
| Audit log | System record of administrative or case-handling actions (who did what, when), supporting traceability and accountability. |
| Audit trail | Time-stamped history of actions, status changes, assignments, communications, and updates for each grievance record. |
| Autoresponder | Configured automated message sent to acknowledge receipt or respond to incoming submissions (often via email). |
| Back-end (case management) | The core system of record where grievance data, workflow states, actions, evidence, and reporting are maintained. |
| Case (grievance record) | A single grievance entry in the e-GRM with a unique reference/ID, metadata, workflow status, assigned owners, and history of actions and communications. |
| Case owner / assignee | The user or team responsible for progressing a grievance at a given workflow stage. |
| Classification | Categorisation of a grievance (e.g., type/category, sensitivity, severity) used to route cases, apply service standards, and drive reporting. |
| Committee (grievance committee) | A designated group that reviews, deliberates, and determines outcomes for grievances requiring formal decision-making, with decisions recorded in the system. |
| Complainant | A person or entity submitting a grievance, complaint, concern, or feedback to the programme. |
| Complaint | A concern raised by a complainant about programme activities, service delivery, risks/impacts, contractor behaviour, or governance issues—captured and managed through the GRM/e-GRM. |
| Configuration | Administrative settings that control system behavior (e.g., forms, roles, routing rules, notification rules, SLA plans). |
| Corrective action | A remedial action assigned and tracked in response to a grievance decision (administrative or operational), often with an owner and due date. |
| Dashboard | A reporting view that summarizes grievance volumes, statuses, performance against service standards, and alerts for operational management and oversight. |
| Data element | A specific field or attribute captured, displayed, or updated by a screen (e.g., status, timestamps, owner, location). |
| Department | An organisational grouping used for routing, permissions, and workload management in the e-GRM configuration. |
| Escalation | Raising a grievance to a higher level (municipal → county → national, or supervisory) due to severity, conflict of interest, request for review, or missed deadlines. |
| Evidence / attachments | Supporting files or information (e.g., photos, documents) linked to a grievance record, stored with appropriate access controls—especially for sensitive cases. |
| Grievance | A complaint, concern, or feedback item related to KUSP2 activities that is received, recorded, processed, resolved, and reported through the GRM. |
| Grievance queue | A saved or configured list/view of grievances (often filtered) used by staff to manage workload and prioritise handling. |
| Help topic | A configured category or entry point that guides how grievances are routed and handled (common in ticketing-style systems). |
| Information governance | Policies and controls for lawful, secure, and appropriate handling of grievance data, including privacy, access control, retention, and reporting. |
| Integration | Connection of the e-GRM to other channels/systems (e.g., email ingestion, SMS notifications, website portal, external referrals) to support multi-channel intake and communication. |
| Jurisdiction | The geographic/organisational boundary (e.g., municipality/county/national) that controls who can access and manage a grievance record. |
| Knowledgebase | A repository of help content and guidance accessible through the system (for staff and/or public users). |
| Low-bandwidth operation | Design approach that supports use in areas with limited connectivity, including simple pages, assisted intake, and resilience measures. |
| Notification | A system-generated or manual message (SMS/email/in-app) used for acknowledgements, updates, reminders, and escalations. |
| Out-of-scope grievance | A submission that is not within the programme’s mandate; recorded for transparency and learning, and the complainant is guided or referred where possible. |
| Portal (public portal) | Public-facing interface linked to the programme website that allows complainants to submit grievances, receive a reference number, and check status where applicable. |
| Privacy notice | Information provided at intake explaining what data is collected, why, and how it will be used and protected. |
| Referral | Directing a grievance (or its handling) to another institution or service provider (especially for sensitive cases), while tracking the referral action in the e-GRM as appropriate. |
| Reporting | Production of registers, summaries, and analytics (monthly/quarterly/annual) to meet oversight and programme requirements and support learning. |
| Role-based access control | Permissions model limiting what users can see or do based on their role (and often jurisdiction), including stricter controls for sensitive cases. |
| Routing rule | Configured logic that directs grievances to the appropriate department/team/owner based on classification, channel, or other attributes. |
| Schedule (SLA schedule) | A defined operating-hours calendar used when calculating SLA timers (e.g., working days/hours). |
| Sensitive case | A grievance requiring restricted access and specialised handling (e.g., SEA/SH, GBV-related cases, fraud and corruption allegations). |
| Service standard | A defined timeframe expectation for key steps (acknowledgement, initial response, resolution) that the system measures and enforces via timers, reminders, and escalations. |
| SLA plan | A configured set of service targets/timers applied to grievances to measure performance and trigger reminders/escalations. |
| Status | A workflow state that indicates where a grievance is in the lifecycle (e.g., received, acknowledged, under investigation, decision issued, closed, under appeal). |
| Status checking | Ability for a complainant to follow up on progress using a reference number (and validation steps), without exposing sensitive information. |
| Template | A pre-defined message or content layout (e.g., email/user templates) used for consistent communications and notices. |
| Triage | Initial assessment and sorting of grievances by type, sensitivity, and severity to determine the handling pathway and urgency. |
| Unique reference number | A system-generated identifier provided to the complainant to reference their grievance for follow-up and tracking. |
| Validation | Rules that prevent incomplete/invalid submissions or configuration states (e.g., required fields, format checks). |
| Workflow | The configured sequence of steps and rules that govern how grievances move from intake through assessment, investigation, decision, corrective action, and closure. |

The definitions are intended to support consistent interpretation of screen labels and workflows across public, agent, and administrative interfaces.
# Executive Summary
This report presents the draft system design for the KUSP2 electronic Grievance Redress Mechanism (e-GRM), expressed primarily through a structured catalogue of user-interface wireframes. The purpose of the report is to translate the wireframes into an implementable specification by documenting screen intent, layout expectations, key interactions, validation rules, minimum data requirements, and access considerations.
The e-GRM is designed to function as a single system of record for programme-related grievances while supporting decentralized handling at county and municipal levels through configurable roles, departments, queues, service level targets, and routing rules. The design supports both self-service and assisted channels, enabling complainants to submit grievances, receive a reference number, and track progress where applicable, while enabling staff to manage the full grievance lifecycle with auditability and reporting.
The wireframe catalogue is organized according to the naming convention of the produced wireframes and is grouped into three main interface areas: (i) the public portal for complainants and general users, (ii) the agent console used for case handling and operational management, and (iii) the administration console used for configuration, oversight, and system governance. Each wireframe is reproduced as a figure and accompanied by a detailed design description to reduce ambiguity during implementation.
Because this is a draft design report, some elements are presented as configurable options rather than fixed requirements. Where the wireframes show legacy wording (for example, 'ticket' terminology), the design assumes the final implementation will align labels consistently with the grievance context.
# 1. Introduction
The Second Kenya Urban Support Program (KUSP2) is a multi-year programme implemented to strengthen urban institutions and improve service delivery across Kenya’s counties and municipalities. A robust grievance redress mechanism is a core accountability tool under the programme, supporting transparency, citizen engagement and timely response to concerns related to programme activities and service delivery.
The electronic grievance redress mechanism (e-GRM) is designed to complement existing grievance handling structures by providing a unified digital platform for intake, tracking, assignment, resolution, and reporting. The system is expected to support multiple intake channels (digital and assisted), maintain a complete history of actions and communications, and provide dashboards and exports to support monitoring and continuous improvement.
This report documents the draft system design based on the approved wireframes. It is intended to be used by technical teams, implementers, and reviewers to validate that the user-interface design is consistent, complete, and implementable.
## 1.1 Purpose of the Report
The purpose of this report is to provide a comprehensive and structured description of the e-GRM user-interface design. It converts the wireframes into a screen-by-screen specification that clarifies intent, required controls, expected behavior, data capture needs, and role-based access expectations.
The report is written to support design validation, implementation planning, and consistency checks across modules. It is not a technical architecture document; rather, it focuses on functional and interaction design as expressed through the wireframes.
## 1.2 Scope
The scope of this report includes the public portal, agent console, and administration console wireframes provided for the e-GRM. For each wireframe, the report provides a descriptive specification that can be used to implement the screen consistently.
Where the wireframes imply supporting services (notifications, routing, SLA timing, audit logs), this report describes the functional behavior at a design level without prescribing a specific technology stack.
## 1.3 Intended Audience
The intended audience includes programme stakeholders responsible for validating the user journey, technical teams responsible for implementation and quality assurance, and operational teams responsible for grievance handling and system administration.
The level of detail is designed to allow each group to confirm that the screen design supports required workflows and governance expectations.
## 1.4 How to Read This Document
The wireframe catalogue is the core of this report. Each wireframe is presented as a figure and is followed by a design description page that explains how the screen is expected to function.
Where this report mentions configuration, it refers to features that are visible in the administration console wireframes (for example help topics, SLA plans, schedules, queues, and notification rules).
# 2. Design Principles
The design principles below guide how the e-GRM should behave across all portals. They are included to ensure that the implementation remains coherent even as configuration values (such as departments, help topics, and SLA plans) evolve over time.
The principles are summarized below to provide a consistent baseline for implementation and review:
User-centred clarity: screens should use plain language, clearly indicate required fields, and provide feedback after actions such as submission, saving, or posting a reply.
Accessibility and inclusion: the interface should be usable with keyboard navigation, readable on low-resolution devices, and support localization (language, date/time formats) consistent with user preferences.
Privacy and confidentiality by design: access to case details should follow a need-to-know model, with special handling for sensitive cases (including SEA/SH) and clear separation of internal notes from external communications.
Workflow traceability: every action that changes a grievance or task (status, assignment, priority, field values) should produce an auditable event that can be reviewed later.
Configurability: routing, forms, SLAs, schedules, and notification rules should be configurable through the administration console to avoid code changes for routine operational updates.
Resilience and performance: queue views, search, and dashboards should remain responsive with large data volumes and under variable network conditions; exports should be generated reliably.
These principles are reflected in the wireframe designs through the consistent use of navigation structures, tabbed configuration areas, queue-based work management, and dedicated log/audit pages. They also inform the behavioral expectations described for each screen in the catalogue.
# 3. System Overview
The e-GRM is organized into three main user-interface areas that correspond to distinct user groups and operational responsibilities. Each area shares common design patterns such as a global header, module navigation, consistent table layouts, and standardized action buttons.
Although the wireframes focus on web interfaces, the design assumes that the system can register grievances from multiple channels by capturing the grievance source (for example web, phone, email, or assisted entry). This allows a unified workflow regardless of intake channel.
## 3.1 Core Modules
The modules below represent the core functional areas visible across the wireframes. They collectively support intake, case handling, internal task tracking, knowledge support, configuration, and oversight.
| Module | Primary Purpose | Primary Users |
| Public Portal | Provide access to guidance content and enable submission and status tracking of grievances. | Public users and complainants |
| Agent Console | Enable staff to manage grievances and tasks, communicate with complainants, and monitor operational performance. | Agents, team leads, department managers |
| Administration Console | Configure the system (forms, routing, SLAs, notifications) and review logs and audit trails. | System administrators and configuration managers |

Each module is described at a high level in this chapter, and the detailed screen specifications are provided in the wireframe catalogue.
## 3.2 High-Level Grievance Lifecycle
The public portal home page illustrates a five-stage grievance resolution process. The system design supports this lifecycle by providing controlled transitions, time tracking, and communication tools.
At implementation time, the specific status names and transitions may be configured. However, the design assumes the following conceptual stages that align with the wireframe narrative.
The lifecycle stages are summarized below:
Receive and acknowledge: a grievance is submitted or registered, a reference is generated, and receipt is communicated to the complainant.
Logging and tracking: the grievance is categorized, routed to the appropriate department or team, and becomes visible in operational queues.
Investigation and enquiry: staff review details, request additional information, create tasks, and coordinate internally using notes and assignments.
Feedback from the team: responses are sent to the complainant through the appropriate channel, and status is updated to reflect progress.
Close out of the grievance: once resolved or otherwise completed, the grievance is closed with a final response and retained for reporting and audit.
The wireframes support these stages through queue-based work management, a detailed grievance thread view, and administrative configuration that defines routing and timing rules.
# 4. Users, Roles and Permissions Model
A clear role and permission model is necessary to ensure confidentiality, prevent unauthorized changes, and enable decentralized grievance handling. The wireframes show role-based separation between the public portal, the agent console, and the administration console, as well as internal permission structures such as teams, roles, and departments.
## 4.1 Role Taxonomy
The table below lists the primary roles implied by the wireframes. The final implementation may introduce additional sub-roles or permission sets; however, these roles provide a baseline mapping between screens and user responsibilities.
| Role | Typical Responsibilities | Primary Screens/Modules |
| Public visitor (guest) | Access public guidance content and submit grievances without creating an account, where allowed. | Public portal: Home, Knowledgebase, Open a New Grievance, Check Status |
| Registered complainant | Submit grievances, track status, and receive notifications via configured channels. | Public portal plus authenticated status views |
| Agent (case handler) | Triage and manage grievances, communicate with complainants, add internal notes, and close cases within assigned scope. | Agent console: grievance queues, grievance detail, new grievance, tasks |
| Team lead / supervisor | Monitor workload, support assignment decisions, oversee response quality, and manage escalations. | Agent console plus dashboards; limited admin functions where permitted |
| Department manager | Oversee grievances within a department, manage routing and escalation practices, and ensure SLA compliance. | Agent console and selected administrative views |
| System administrator | Configure system settings, forms, SLAs, queues, notifications, and user access; review logs and audit trails. | Administration console |
| Auditor (read-only) | Review audit logs and reports without performing operational actions. | Administration console: audit logs, reports/exports (where enabled) |

Role-based access control should be enforced consistently. For example, internal notes must never be visible to public users, and configuration pages must be restricted to authorized administrators.
## 4.2 Sensitive and Confidential Case Handling
Some grievances may require heightened confidentiality, including cases related to SEA/SH or other sensitive matters. The design supports confidentiality through a combination of routing, restricted visibility, and separation of internal notes from external communications.
At implementation time, confidentiality controls should include: (i) restricted queues for sensitive categories, (ii) limited participant/collaborator visibility, (iii) redaction of personal details in lists and exports when required, and (iv) enhanced audit logging for access and actions.
# 5. Information Architecture and Data Model
The wireframes imply a structured information architecture that combines core grievance attributes, configurable classification elements, and optional custom fields. This chapter describes the conceptual data model needed to implement the screens consistently, focusing on the minimum data elements visible in the interface.
## 5.1 Core Entities
The e-GRM uses a set of core entities that appear repeatedly across queues, detail views, and administrative configuration screens. Understanding these entities helps ensure that form fields, reports, and exports remain consistent.
| Entity | Description | Examples of Screens |
| Grievance | Primary case record capturing the issue, status, routing, SLA, and full communication thread. | Public new grievance, grievance queues, grievance detail view |
| User | Identity record for a complainant or a staff user, including contact details and authentication attributes. | User directory, user profile, agent profile |
| Organization | Optional grouping of users (for example institutional complainants) with account managers. | Organizations list and organization details |
| Task | Internal work item linked to a grievance to coordinate activities and deadlines. | Task queues, task detail, grievance tasks tab |
| Department | Routing and permission container controlling who can view and manage grievances. | Department settings and access pages; assignment dropdowns |
| Help Topic | Classification used to drive routing, default values, and dynamic form fields. | Public and agent new grievance forms; help topic management |
| SLA Plan and Schedule | Time targets and calendars used to compute due dates and overdue states. | SLA management, schedules management, grievance metadata panels |
| Queue / Filter | Saved criteria defining list views for grievances or tasks. | Queue tabs, grievance queues configuration, filters management |
| Knowledgebase Article | Published guidance content used to reduce grievances and support users. | Knowledgebase pages and management screens |

These entities provide the structural foundation for all screens. Administrative configuration screens are used to manage the values and rules associated with each entity.
## 5.2 Attachments and Evidence Handling
Attachments appear in grievance submission forms, reply editors, internal notes, and task forms. The design assumes attachments are stored securely, linked to the specific thread entry or task record, and subject to size and type limits configurable by administrators.
For auditability, the system should record who uploaded each attachment, when it was uploaded, the associated grievance or task, and whether the attachment is visible to the complainant or restricted to staff.
# 6. Workflow Design
The wireframes show a workflow-driven system in which grievances and tasks move through statuses, assignments, and queues. This chapter describes the key workflow concepts implied by the interface so that behavior is implemented consistently across screens.
## 6.1 Assignment, Routing and Escalation
Assignment and routing are supported through help topics, departments, teams, and configurable filters. The agent console provides bulk assignment controls, while the administration console provides configuration screens for queues and routing rules.
SLA plans and schedules drive due dates and overdue states. Overdue queues and alerts are visible in the agent console and configurable through the administration console.
## 6.2 Communication Model
The grievance detail view separates external replies from internal notes. External replies are sent to the complainant and permitted participants based on notification rules, while internal notes support staff collaboration and are restricted by role.
This separation is critical for confidentiality and should be enforced at both the user-interface and data layers.
# 7. Configuration and Administration Model
The administration console wireframes show a comprehensive set of configuration areas for system governance. These include company and site information, system settings, grievance settings, task settings, user and agent management, email configuration, knowledgebase management, and diagnostic/logging functions.
## 7.1 Configuration Domains
The top navigation and tab structure indicates a domain-based configuration approach. Each domain contains sub-pages for specific object types or settings, enabling administrators to update routing, forms, SLAs, and notifications without changing code.
The wireframe catalogue provides the screen-level design for these configuration pages, including expected controls and behaviors.
# 8. Wireframe Catalogue
This chapter catalogues each wireframe provided for the e-GRM. The order follows the naming convention of the wireframe files and is grouped by major interface area. For each wireframe, the figure is followed by a design description page that clarifies intent, UI structure, interactions, data elements, and implementation notes.
## 8.1 Public Portal and Complainant Interface (Wireframes 0.x)
The public portal wireframes represent the self-service interface used by complainants and the general public. The portal provides access to guidance content, training resources, grievance submission, and status tracking.
The design emphasizes clarity, accessibility, and secure access to grievance information. The public portal should remain usable under low-bandwidth conditions and should support multiple languages where configured.
## 8.2 Agent Console for Case Handling (Wireframes 1.x)
The agent console wireframes represent the staff-facing interface used for daily grievance and task management. The core design pattern is a queue-based workbench with filters, bulk actions, and a detailed case view for communication and collaboration.
The agent console must enforce role-based access and confidentiality rules while remaining efficient for high-volume operations. The wireframes show dashboards, directories, advanced search, and account preferences that support operational performance.
## 8.3 Administration Console for Configuration and Oversight (Wireframes 2.x)
The administration console wireframes represent the configuration and oversight environment. Administrators can define help topics, forms, routing filters, SLA plans and schedules, notification settings, teams and roles, email settings, and knowledgebase content.
The administration console also provides operational transparency through system logs, audit logs, and diagnostic information screens. Changes made through these screens must be recorded in audit logs and protected by strict permissions.
### 8.1.1 Wireframe 0.1 - Home
Figure 1: 0.1 - Home
Wireframe 0.1 - Home belongs to the Public Portal and is intended to support the workflow implied by the screen name 'Home'. The primary users of this screen are Public visitors, guest users, registered complainants, and assisted-intake staff (where applicable).
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Global header with public navigation links (Knowledgebase, Open a New Grievance, Check Grievance Status) and sign-in entry point.
Hero/welcome panel that explains the purpose of the e-GRM and sets expectations for how grievances are handled.
Self-service shortcuts (for example, user guide link and training access) to reduce repeat questions and improve first-time success.
Process overview tiles that visually represent the end-to-end grievance lifecycle stages.
Search bar to quickly locate knowledgebase articles or guidance content.
Primary call-to-action cards for submitting a new grievance and checking an existing grievance status.
Featured knowledgebase articles section to highlight the most used or most important guidance items.
Footer with cookie notice, copyright statement, and platform attribution.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Selecting 'Open a New Grievance' routes the user to the public grievance submission form; if a user is signed in, profile data can be pre-filled to reduce data entry.
Selecting 'Check Grievance Status' routes the user to the status access workflow; the system must enforce secure access (for example email link or authenticated session).
Search submissions query knowledgebase content and return results without exposing case data.
Training links open the learning catalogue and preserve the user-selected language for continuity.
Featured articles can be curated by administrators and must respect publication status and language settings.
Cookie notice acknowledgement should only store non-personal session markers consistent with the footer statement.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Primary record identifier | Label / table column | System | Unique ID used for navigation and linking. |
| Primary status | Label / dropdown | System/Staff | Drives workflow state and visibility. |
| Created / updated timestamps | Labels | System | Used for audit and sorting. |
| Owner / assignee | Label / dropdown | System/Staff | Supports accountability and workload management. |
| Notes / comments | Text area | User/Staff | Captured with audit trail as configured. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.
### 8.1.2 Wireframe 0.1.1 - Sign-in
Figure 2: 0.1.1 - Sign-in
Wireframe 0.1.1 - Sign-in belongs to the Public Portal and is intended to authenticate the user and establish an authorized session for the relevant portal. The primary users of this screen are Public visitors, guest users, registered complainants, and assisted-intake staff (where applicable).
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Authentication panel with username/email input, password input, and a primary 'Sign in' or 'Log in' button.
Contextual guidance panel that routes users to the correct portal (public user vs agent/admin) and offers next steps.
Support links such as account creation, password reset, and alternative submission options where applicable.
Standard header and footer elements to maintain brand consistency and legal notices.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Credentials are validated against the configured authentication store and, where enabled, trigger a second factor challenge before establishing a session.
Incorrect credentials must return a generic error message to avoid account enumeration and must be logged for security monitoring.
Account lockout and throttling rules apply after repeated failures and are reflected in system logs.
Successful authentication routes the user to the correct landing page for their role and portal (public, agent, or admin).
Links such as account creation or agent sign-in must maintain clear separation of public and staff authentication endpoints.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Username / Email | Text input | User | Required; validated against configured identity store. |
| Password | Password input | User | Required; never stored in plaintext; subject to lockout rules. |
| Second Factor Token | OTP input (conditional) | User | Displayed only when 2FA is enabled for the account/role. |
| Session ID | System-managed | System | Generated after authentication; stored securely with timeout. |
| Login Attempt Log | System-managed | System | Records outcome, timestamp, IP; visible in system logs. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.
### 8.1.3 Wireframe 0.1.2 - Go to Training
Figure 3: 0.1.2 - Go to Training
Wireframe 0.1.2 - Go to Training belongs to the Public Portal and is intended to provide self-guided learning content and supporting materials to improve correct usage of the e-GRM. The primary users of this screen are Public visitors, guest users, registered complainants, and assisted-intake staff (where applicable).
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Global header consistent with the public portal, including the language selector and navigation.
Training catalogue grid/list with course cards that include title, short description, and a 'start' action.
Search and filter controls (for example by topic or audience) to help users locate relevant learning content.
Language selector to switch learning content language at runtime.
Footer area with standard notices and attribution.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Selecting a training module opens its detail view and remembers the learner’s position when they return, subject to user/session state.
Language selection updates visible training titles and content where translated assets are available.
Search and filters narrow the module list in real time and should be usable on low-bandwidth connections.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Training module | Card / viewer | System | Represents a training asset with language variants. |
| Selected language | Dropdown | User | Controls which asset variant is loaded. |
| Progress position | System-managed | System/User | Stored per user where authenticated; session-based otherwise. |
| Accessibility settings | Player controls | User | Captions and speed are stored per user/session. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.

Playback controls (play/pause, speed, captions) to support different learning preferences and accessibility needs.

Secondary resources panel that links to additional guidance material (for example training or contact channels).
Footer with standard notices.

| Article | Link/list item | System | Published content with versioning and attachments. |
| Feedback rating | Optional control | User | If enabled, captures article usefulness metrics. |

### 8.1.6 Wireframe 0.3 - Open a New Grievance
Figure 6: 0.3 - Open a New Grievance
Wireframe 0.3 - Open a New Grievance belongs to the Public Portal and is intended to allow a complainant to submit a new grievance through the public-facing interface and receive a reference number for tracking. The primary users of this screen are Public visitors, guest users, registered complainants, and assisted-intake staff (where applicable).
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Contact information section capturing complainant details (email, full name, phone) for follow-up.
Help Topic selector to classify the grievance and drive routing, SLA, and form fields.
Project context selector to associate the grievance with the relevant county/municipality/project component.
Issue summary field to capture a short, searchable description of the grievance.
Rich text description editor for detailed narrative, including formatting support.
Attachment upload control for evidence and supporting documents.
Primary action buttons to create/submit the grievance and secondary actions to reset or cancel.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Required fields must be validated client-side and server-side; invalid submissions must highlight missing or incorrect fields clearly.
On submission, the system generates a unique grievance reference number and displays a confirmation screen and/or sends a receipt notification to the provided contact channel.
Help Topic selection drives additional form fields and routing rules (department, SLA) as configured by administrators.
Attachments must be validated for file type and size limits and stored securely with malware scanning where available.
Where enabled, CAPTCHA/human verification is enforced to reduce automated submissions.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Complainant email | Text input | User | Required; used for notifications and secure status access. |
| Complainant full name | Text input | User | Optional/required per policy; supports anonymization settings. |
| Phone number | Text input | User | Optional; supports SMS/voice follow-up where configured. |
| Help Topic | Dropdown | Configured list | Required; drives routing, form, SLA defaults. |
| Project context | Dropdown | Configured list | Required where enabled; links case to location/component. |
| Issue summary | Text input | User | Required; becomes the grievance subject for search and reporting. |
| Description | Rich text editor | User | Required; stored as first thread entry. |
| Attachments | File upload | User | Optional; enforced by size/type limits and malware scanning where available. |
| Grievance reference | System-generated | System | Assigned on successful submission and communicated to user. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.
### 8.1.7 Wireframe 0.4 - Check Grievance Status
Figure 7: 0.4 - Check Grievance Status
Wireframe 0.4 - Check Grievance Status belongs to the Public Portal and is intended to allow a complainant to request secure access to the status of a previously submitted grievance using their email and reference number. The primary users of this screen are Public visitors, guest users, registered complainants, and assisted-intake staff (where applicable).
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Email input field to identify the complainant requesting status access.
Grievance number/reference input field to locate the grievance in the system.
Primary action to request an email access link (or similar secure method) to view grievance status.
Information panel explaining alternatives such as account sign-in or how to obtain the reference number.
Footer with standard notices.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
The combination of email and grievance reference is validated; if valid, the system sends a secure access link to the email address.
Status access must not disclose sensitive information unless the requester is authenticated and authorized for the case.
Invalid requests must return a generic message (for example, 'If a matching record exists, an email will be sent') to avoid information leakage.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Complainant email | Text input | User | Used to send secure access link. |
| Grievance reference | Text input | User | Validated; not disclosed back to user if invalid. |
| Access token | Email link (system) | System | Time-limited; single-use where configured. |
| Access audit | System-managed | System | Logs access requests and views for security. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.

Primary action to register and secondary action to cancel and return to the previous page.
Footer with standard notices.

Password rules are enforced (minimum length, complexity, reuse restrictions) and failures show actionable guidance.
Time zone and locale choices determine how dates/times appear and how notifications are timestamped.

| Time zone | Dropdown + auto-detect | User/System | Defaulted using browser when permitted. |
| Password | Password input | User | Required; policy enforced. |
| Account status | System-managed | System | Pending until verification; then active. |

### 8.2.1 Wireframe 1.1 - Home (Open)
Figure 9: 1.1 - Home (Open)
Wireframe 1.1 - Home (Open) belongs to the Agent Console and is intended to provide a filtered queue view for grievances, specifically the 'Home (Open)' queue, enabling rapid triage and workload management. The primary users of this screen are Case handlers (agents), team leads, and department managers operating the agent console.
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Global header with module navigation and user utilities (profile, theme toggle, sign out).
Queue navigation tabs that switch between major grievance views (Open, My grievances, Closed, Search, New Grievance).
Queue title area showing the current queue/filter context (for example 'Home (Open)').
Search bar for quick filtering by grievance number, subject, or submitter.
Bulk action toolbar for multi-select operations (assign, transfer, set priority/status, export, delete) subject to permissions.
Tabular grievance list including key columns such as ID, last updated, subject, submitter, priority, and assigned agent/team.
Pagination and row selection controls (All/None/Toggle) for efficient list management.
Export option to produce CSV/PDF outputs aligned with role permissions and reporting needs.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Selecting one or more rows enables bulk actions; actions must be permission-checked per grievance and per action.
Clicking a grievance reference or subject opens the grievance detail view in the same window (or new tab if configured).
Queue membership is dynamic and reflects grievance status, assignment, SLA state (overdue), and configured filters.
Search uses quick matching for common terms; advanced search is available for complex queries and saved searches.
Export outputs the current queue view and respects column configuration and data redaction rules for sensitive cases.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Grievance reference | Table column / link | System | Clickable; opens grievance detail view. |
| Last updated | Table column | System | Derived from latest thread activity or metadata change. |
| Subject / summary | Table column | System | Indexed for search; typically from issue summary. |
| Submitter | Table column | User/System | Redacted where case is marked confidential. |
| Priority | Table column | System/Staff | Controls SLA urgency and escalation visibility. |
| Assigned to | Table column | System/Staff | Agent or team currently responsible. |
| Queue filter label | Header label | System | Reflects the configured queue criteria. |
| Export dataset | Export action | System | Includes only visible columns and permitted data fields. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.

### 8.2.4 Wireframe 1.1.1.3 - Grievance Case Management - Thread - Post Internal Note
Figure 12: 1.1.1.3 - Grievance Case Management - Thread - Post Internal Note
Wireframe 1.1.1.3 - Grievance Case Management - Thread - Post Internal Note belongs to the Agent Console and is intended to provide a complete, end-to-end view of a single grievance, including metadata, conversation thread, internal notes, tasks, and workflow controls. The primary users of this screen are Case handlers (agents), team leads, and department managers operating the agent console.
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Grievance header showing reference number, current status, and quick actions.
Summary panel capturing priority, department, creation timestamp, and SLA/due information.
Complainant panel containing identity and contact details, including collaborator management where enabled.
Grievance details panel showing the configured form fields, including project context and classification.
Thread view showing the chronological sequence of external messages and internal notes, with system events clearly distinguished.
Reply composer supporting recipients, canned responses, rich text editing, attachments, and status update controls.
Internal note composer for non-public collaboration content, including attachments and visibility controls.
Tasks tab to manage and view internal tasks linked to the grievance for coordinated resolution.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Posting a reply adds a new external message to the grievance thread and triggers configured notifications to the submitter and permitted participants.
Posting an internal note adds a private entry visible only to authorized staff roles and is not sent to the complainant.
Changing status, priority, help topic, or assignment updates grievance metadata, triggers any configured routing rules, and records an audit event.
Attachments on replies or notes are validated and linked to the corresponding thread entry, preserving a full evidence trail.
The SLA due date is recalculated based on status transitions and the selected SLA plan and schedule, and overdue states are flagged automatically.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Grievance reference | Header label | System | Unique identifier; immutable. |
| Status | Dropdown / label | Staff | Controls workflow state and queue membership. |
| Priority | Dropdown / label | Staff | May be restricted for some roles; audited. |
| Department | Dropdown / label | System/Staff | Routing container; impacts permissions and visibility. |
| Help Topic | Dropdown | System/Staff | May change required fields; change is audited. |
| SLA plan and due date | Labels / dropdown | System | Computed based on schedule; overdue triggers alerts. |
| Thread messages | Thread timeline | User/Staff | Immutable entries; edits follow policy and audit. |
| Internal notes | Internal note thread | Staff | Visible only to permitted roles; audited. |
| Attachments | Attachment list/upload | User/Staff | Stored securely; linked to thread entries; scanned where available. |
| Audit events | Timeline entries | System | Captures assignment, status changes, and key actions. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.
### 8.2.4.1 Wireframe 1.1.1.3.1 - Grievance Case Management - Thread - Post Reply
Figure 12a: 1.1.1.3.1 - Grievance Case Management - Thread - Post Reply
Wireframe 1.1.1.3.1 - Grievance Case Management - Thread - Post Reply belongs to the Agent Console and is intended to provide a complete, end-to-end view of a single grievance, including metadata, conversation thread, internal notes, tasks, and workflow controls. The primary users of this screen are Case handlers (agents), team leads, and department managers operating the agent console.
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Grievance header and metadata panels showing status, priority, department, assigned team, and key timestamps.
Grievance Thread view presenting the chronological conversation and system events for the case.
Composer toggle tabs (Post Reply / Post Internal Note) with Post Reply as the active state.
Reply composer fields including sender (From), recipients (complainant and collaborators), and Reply To options.
Canned response selection, rich-text response editor, and attachment upload area.
Optional response suggestions, signature selection, and grievance status update control.
Primary actions to Post Reply and Reset.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Selecting recipients/collaborators updates who will receive the outgoing message and is validated against access rules.
Choosing a canned response pre-populates the editor; users may edit text and add attachments before posting.
Posting a reply creates an external thread entry, updates last response metadata, and triggers configured notifications.
Reset clears unsaved changes without affecting the underlying grievance record.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.

Grievance header and metadata panels providing context for the active case.
Tabbed workspace with Grievance Thread and Tasks tabs, with Tasks as the active view.
Tasks panel showing the task list for the grievance or an empty-state message when no tasks exist.
Add New Task action to create and link a task to the grievance.
Pagination/scrolling controls for long task lists (where applicable).
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Switching to the Tasks tab loads tasks associated with the grievance and displays current status and ownership.
Selecting Add New Task opens the task creation workflow and links the new task back to the grievance.
Task updates (e.g., completion, reassignment, due-date changes) are recorded in the audit log and reflected in the task list.
Empty-state messaging guides users when a grievance has no tasks.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.

### 8.2.5 Wireframe 1.1.2.1 - My Grievance
Figure 13: 1.1.2.1 - My Grievance
Wireframe 1.1.2.1 - My Grievance belongs to the Agent Console and is intended to provide a filtered queue view for grievances, specifically the 'My Grievance' queue, enabling rapid triage and workload management. The primary users of this screen are Case handlers (agents), team leads, and department managers operating the agent console.
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Global header with module navigation and user utilities (profile, theme toggle, sign out).
Queue navigation tabs that switch between major grievance views (Open, My grievances, Closed, Search, New Grievance).
Queue title area showing the current queue/filter context (for example 'My Grievance').
Search bar for quick filtering by grievance number, subject, or submitter.
Bulk action toolbar for multi-select operations (assign, transfer, set priority/status, export, delete) subject to permissions.
Tabular grievance list including key columns such as ID, last updated, subject, submitter, priority, and assigned agent/team.
Pagination and row selection controls (All/None/Toggle) for efficient list management.
Export option to produce CSV/PDF outputs aligned with role permissions and reporting needs.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Selecting one or more rows enables bulk actions; actions must be permission-checked per grievance and per action.
Clicking a grievance reference or subject opens the grievance detail view in the same window (or new tab if configured).
Queue membership is dynamic and reflects grievance status, assignment, SLA state (overdue), and configured filters.
Search uses quick matching for common terms; advanced search is available for complex queries and saved searches.
Export outputs the current queue view and respects column configuration and data redaction rules for sensitive cases.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Grievance reference | Table column / link | System | Clickable; opens grievance detail view. |
| Last updated | Table column | System | Derived from latest thread activity or metadata change. |
| Subject / summary | Table column | System | Indexed for search; typically from issue summary. |
| Submitter | Table column | User/System | Redacted where case is marked confidential. |
| Priority | Table column | System/Staff | Controls SLA urgency and escalation visibility. |
| Assigned to | Table column | System/Staff | Agent or team currently responsible. |
| Queue filter label | Header label | System | Reflects the configured queue criteria. |
| Export dataset | Export action | System | Includes only visible columns and permitted data fields. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.

When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Selecting one or more rows enables bulk actions; actions must be permission-checked per grievance and per action.
Clicking a grievance reference or subject opens the grievance detail view in the same window (or new tab if configured).
Queue membership is dynamic and reflects grievance status, assignment, SLA state (overdue), and configured filters.
Search uses quick matching for common terms; advanced search is available for complex queries and saved searches.
Export outputs the current queue view and respects column configuration and data redaction rules for sensitive cases.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Grievance reference | Table column / link | System | Clickable; opens grievance detail view. |
| Last updated | Table column | System | Derived from latest thread activity or metadata change. |
| Subject / summary | Table column | System | Indexed for search; typically from issue summary. |
| Submitter | Table column | User/System | Redacted where case is marked confidential. |
| Priority | Table column | System/Staff | Controls SLA urgency and escalation visibility. |
| Assigned to | Table column | System/Staff | Agent or team currently responsible. |
| Queue filter label | Header label | System | Reflects the configured queue criteria. |
| Export dataset | Export action | System | Includes only visible columns and permitted data fields. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.

### 8.2.16 Wireframe 1.1.4.1 - Advanced Grievance Search (Criteria)
Figure 24: 1.1.4.1 - Advanced Grievance Search (Criteria)
Wireframe 1.1.4.1 - Advanced Grievance Search (Criteria) belongs to the Agent Console and is intended to support the workflow implied by the screen name 'Advanced Grievance Search (Criteria)'. The primary users of this screen are Case handlers (agents), team leads, and department managers operating the agent console.
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Tabbed advanced search configuration including criteria definition and column selection.
Field selection controls to add, remove, and reorder search filters used to query grievances.
Operator and value inputs supporting precise search (for example equals, contains, date ranges).
Column selection area controlling which data points appear in the search results table.
Save search controls to store commonly used searches as reusable queues, subject to permissions.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Criteria additions immediately affect the executed query once saved; unsaved changes do not impact other users.
Column configuration controls the results table and any exported output for the saved search/queue.
Saving a search creates a reusable queue entry that can be private to the user or shared (subject to role permissions).
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.

| Primary status | Label / dropdown | System/Staff | Drives workflow state and visibility. |
| Created / updated timestamps | Labels | System | Used for audit and sorting. |
| Owner / assignee | Label / dropdown | System/Staff | Supports accountability and workload management. |
| Notes / comments | Text area | User/Staff | Captured with audit trail as configured. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.

Wireframe 1.1.5 - New Grievance belongs to the Agent Console and is intended to allow authorized staff to register a new grievance on behalf of a complainant (including assisted channels such as phone or in-person) and initiate the workflow. The primary users of this screen are Case handlers (agents), team leads, and department managers operating the agent console.
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
User lookup/selection control to associate the grievance with an existing user or create a new user record.
CC/participants and collaborator controls for multi-party cases, where permitted by role and confidentiality settings.
Grievance metadata configuration (source channel, help topic, department, SLA plan, due date) to drive workflow.
Assignment controls to allocate the grievance to an agent or a team and optionally set priority.
Grievance details section (summary, description, project context, attachments) using the configured form.
Response and internal note editors to record initial acknowledgement and internal context at creation time.
Primary action buttons to open the grievance, reset the form, or cancel.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
The screen should enforce role-based access control and validate user input consistently.
All changes and submissions should be logged appropriately to support audit and troubleshooting.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| User record | Lookup/create control | Staff | Required; links grievance to a user entity. |
| Source channel | Dropdown | Staff | Required; options include web, phone, email, in-person, etc. |
| Help Topic | Dropdown | Configured list | Required; drives routing and form fields. |
| Department | Dropdown | Configured list | Defaults from help topic; override subject to permissions. |
| SLA plan | Dropdown | Configured list | Defaults from help topic/department; sets due date logic. |
| Due date | Date/time picker | System/Staff | Calculated from SLA; manual override optional with permission. |
| Assignee (agent/team) | Dropdown | Staff | Optional; can be auto-assigned by filters. |
| Summary and description | Text + rich editor | Staff/User | Captures the case narrative; stored in thread. |
| Initial internal note | Rich text editor | Staff | Optional; internal-only context; audited. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.
