### 8.2.23 Wireframe 1.2.1 - Dashboard
Figure 31: 1.2.1 - Dashboard
Wireframe 1.2.1 - Dashboard belongs to the Agent Console and is intended to provide a monitoring dashboard with charts and summary tables supporting operational oversight and reporting. The primary users of this screen are Case handlers (agents), team leads, and department managers operating the agent console.
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Global agent navigation menu providing access to Dashboard, Users, Tasks, Grievances, and Knowledgebase.
Timeframe filters to change the reporting period (for example Today, This Week, This Month, Custom).
Activity chart visualizing grievance volume trends and throughput across the selected period.
Statistics table with tabs for Department, Topic, and Agent performance breakdown.
Export control to download aggregated statistics for reporting and offline analysis.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Timeframe controls refresh both the chart and the statistics table consistently so figures remain comparable.
Export creates a downloadable report (CSV/PDF) using the current filters and includes only data within the user’s permission scope.
Dashboard statistics must compute metrics consistently (opened, assigned, overdue, closed, reopened, deleted, service time, response time).
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Reporting period | Timeframe selector | User | Controls aggregation window for all metrics. |
| Grievance counts | Chart + table | System | Derived from grievance records and statuses. |
| Overdue count | Table metric | System | Computed using SLA due dates and current time. |
| Service time | Table metric | System | Elapsed time from open to close (per policy). |
| Response time | Table metric | System | Elapsed time to first response (per policy). |
| Export output | Export action | System | Downloads aggregated dataset in configured format. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.

### 8.2.28 Wireframe 1.2.3.1 - My Account Profile
Figure 36: 1.2.3.1 - My Account Profile
Wireframe 1.2.3.1 - My Account Profile belongs to the Agent Console and is intended to support the workflow implied by the screen name 'My Account Profile'. The primary users of this screen are Authenticated case handlers (agents) and supervisory users with staff access.
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Profile header identifying the currently authenticated user and account context.
Tabbed navigation across account settings (Account, Preferences, Signature, Dark Mode).
Editable fields for identity, authentication options, notification preferences, and localization settings.
Save, reset, and cancel controls to manage changes safely.
Contextual help text and tooltips for settings with policy implications (for example 2FA and password).
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Edits to profile information require validation and, where relevant, re-verification (for example email address changes).
Authentication settings such as 2FA changes require the user to confirm their current password or re-authenticate.
Preference changes (pagination, refresh rate, default queue) apply immediately and persist per user account.
Signature changes affect outgoing messages composed from the grievance thread or task updates depending on configuration.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.

When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Required fields (category, listing type, question, and answer) are validated before allowing save.
Selecting Attachments or Internal Notes switches tabs without losing unsaved content in the current session.
Adding the FAQ persists the article and makes it available for use according to its listing type and publication settings.
Reset reverts unsaved edits; Cancel exits the workflow without creating the article.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.

### 8.3.1 Wireframe 2.0 - Log in
Figure 50: 2.0 - Log in
Wireframe 2.0 - Log in belongs to the Administration Console and is intended to authenticate the user and establish an authorized session for the relevant portal. The primary users of this screen are System administrators and configuration managers with administrative access rights.
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Authentication panel with username/email input, password input, and a primary 'Sign in' or 'Log in' button.
Contextual guidance panel that routes users to the correct portal (public user vs agent/admin) and offers next steps.
Support links such as account creation, password reset, and alternative submission options where applicable.
Standard header and footer elements to maintain brand consistency and legal notices.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Credentials are validated against the configured authentication store and, where enabled, trigger a second factor challenge before establishing a session.
Incorrect credentials must return a generic error message to avoid account enumeration and must be logged for security monitoring.
Account lockout and throttling rules apply after repeated failures and are reflected in system logs.
Successful authentication routes the user to the correct landing page for their role and portal (public, agent, or admin).
Links such as account creation or agent sign-in must maintain clear separation of public and staff authentication endpoints.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Username / Email | Text input | User | Required; validated against configured identity store. |
| Password | Password input | User | Required; never stored in plaintext; subject to lockout rules. |
| Second Factor Token | OTP input (conditional) | User | Displayed only when 2FA is enabled for the account/role. |
| Session ID | System-managed | System | Generated after authentication; stored securely with timeout. |
| Login Attempt Log | System-managed | System | Records outcome, timestamp, IP; visible in system logs. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.

| Actor / IP address | Table column | System | Captured automatically for traceability. |
| Export dataset | Export action | System | Produces an immutable copy for review. |

Reset/Cancel actions revert unsaved changes to prevent accidental misconfiguration.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Configuration key | Form field label | System | Represents a distinct configurable option. |
| Configuration value | Input / checkbox / dropdown | Admin | Validated; may be scoped (global/department/email). |
| Scope | Implicit / label | System | Determines precedence when overrides exist. |
| Effective date/time | System-managed | System | Used when settings are staged or applied immediately. |
| Changed by | System-managed | System | Stored for audit and displayed in audit logs. |
| Changed on | System-managed | System | Timestamp of change; displayed in audit logs. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.

Saving changes updates system-wide defaults and records an administrative audit entry with actor and timestamp.
Where indicated, settings may be overridden at department or email level; the UI should indicate override precedence clearly.
Enabling/disabling alerts and autoresponders changes who receives notifications for new grievances, messages, and overdue conditions.
Queue configuration defines default queue availability and ordering in the agent console.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.

Tasks settings interface controlling default behavior and options for task workflow.

Save Changes and Reset Changes actions with audit logging.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Task settings define default task workflow and must be applied consistently across the agent panel.
Changes are audited and may require a cache refresh to reflect in all sessions.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.

### 8.3.38 Wireframe 2.3.3 - SLA

Wireframe 2.3.3 - SLA belongs to the Administration Console and is intended to support configuration and administration of the system feature represented by the screen 'SLA'. The primary users of this screen are System administrators and configuration managers with administrative access rights.
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Management list page with a table of configurable objects (for example Help Topics, Filters, SLA Plans, Schedules, Forms, Lists, Pages, API keys).
Primary action to add a new item and a secondary 'More' menu for bulk operations.
Row-level controls such as enable/disable, edit, and ordering where applicable.
Pagination and, where relevant, export controls.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Add/edit actions open the corresponding configuration form; save applies changes and updates dependent routing/SLA behavior.
Disable/delete actions must require confirmation and must protect system-critical defaults from accidental removal.
Ordering controls affect how items appear in dropdowns and routing logic, and must be preserved consistently.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Configuration key | Form field label | System | Represents a distinct configurable option. |
| Configuration value | Input / checkbox / dropdown | Admin | Validated; may be scoped (global/department/email). |
| Scope | Implicit / label | System | Determines precedence when overrides exist. |
| Effective date/time | System-managed | System | Used when settings are staged or applied immediately. |
| Changed by | System-managed | System | Stored for audit and displayed in audit logs. |
| Changed on | System-managed | System | Timestamp of change; displayed in audit logs. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.

Contextual help markers/tooltips supporting correct configuration by administrators.

All configuration changes require appropriate administrative privileges and are recorded in the audit log.
Validation must prevent invalid configuration states (for example missing required fields, invalid email formats, or conflicting rules).
Reset/Cancel actions revert unsaved changes to prevent accidental misconfiguration.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.

When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Add/edit actions open the corresponding configuration form; save applies changes and updates dependent routing/SLA behavior.
Disable/delete actions must require confirmation and must protect system-critical defaults from accidental removal.
Ordering controls affect how items appear in dropdowns and routing logic, and must be preserved consistently.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Configuration key | Form field label | System | Represents a distinct configurable option. |
| Configuration value | Input / checkbox / dropdown | Admin | Validated; may be scoped (global/department/email). |
| Scope | Implicit / label | System | Determines precedence when overrides exist. |
| Effective date/time | System-managed | System | Used when settings are staged or applied immediately. |
| Changed by | System-managed | System | Stored for audit and displayed in audit logs. |
| Changed on | System-managed | System | Timestamp of change; displayed in audit logs. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.

All configuration changes require appropriate administrative privileges and are recorded in the audit log.
Validation must prevent invalid configuration states (for example missing required fields, invalid email formats, or conflicting rules).
Reset/Cancel actions revert unsaved changes to prevent accidental misconfiguration.

| Changed by | System-managed | System | Stored for audit and displayed in audit logs. |
| Changed on | System-managed | System | Timestamp of change; displayed in audit logs. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.

Email configuration changes affect inbound parsing, outbound sender identity, and notification routing and must be tested before production use.

Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.

Primary actions (Add, Save, Update) and secondary actions (Reset, Cancel, Back) as applicable.
Contextual help markers/tooltips supporting correct configuration by administrators.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.

All configuration changes require appropriate administrative privileges and are recorded in the audit log.
Validation must prevent invalid configuration states (for example missing required fields, invalid email formats, or conflicting rules).
Reset/Cancel actions revert unsaved changes to prevent accidental misconfiguration.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.

Validation must prevent invalid configuration states (for example missing required fields, invalid email formats, or conflicting rules).
Reset/Cancel actions revert unsaved changes to prevent accidental misconfiguration.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.
| Data element | UI control / location | Source / owner | Notes and validation |
| Configuration key | Form field label | System | Represents a distinct configurable option. |
| Configuration value | Input / checkbox / dropdown | Admin | Validated; may be scoped (global/department/email). |
| Scope | Implicit / label | System | Determines precedence when overrides exist. |
| Effective date/time | System-managed | System | Used when settings are staged or applied immediately. |
| Changed by | System-managed | System | Stored for audit and displayed in audit logs. |
| Changed on | System-managed | System | Timestamp of change; displayed in audit logs. |

Where a data element is configured through the administration console (for example help topics, SLA plans, departments, and notification rules), the values shown in the wireframe are illustrative and should be treated as configurable parameters.
Implementation note: If the screen contains legacy terminology (for example 'ticket'), the final user-facing labels should be normalized to 'grievance' for consistency. All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.

All date/time fields should respect the user’s configured time zone, and all actions that modify records or configuration should generate an auditable event.
### 8.3.80 Wireframe 2.5.3.1 - Definition
Figure 129: 2.5.3.1 - Definition
Wireframe 2.5.3.1 - Definition belongs to the Administration Console and is intended to support configuration and administration of the system feature represented by the screen 'Definition'. The primary users of this screen are System administrators and configuration managers with administrative access rights.
The wireframe image on the previous page should be treated as the authoritative reference for layout and visible controls. This design description specifies expected behavior, minimum data requirements, validation, and role-based access considerations so that implementation remains consistent across portals and environments.
The user-interface components and layout regions on this screen are summarized below. These items describe what must be visible and how information is organized, while allowing for responsive behavior and minor visual refinements during implementation.
Administrative header and navigation showing the current configuration domain and available modules.
Contextual sub-navigation tabs for the active domain (for example Company, System, Grievance, Tasks, Agents, Users, Knowledgebase, Theme).
Main configuration panel consisting of a form or a management table, depending on the page purpose.
Primary actions (Add, Save, Update) and secondary actions (Reset, Cancel, Back) as applicable.
Contextual help markers/tooltips supporting correct configuration by administrators.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
All configuration changes require appropriate administrative privileges and are recorded in the audit log.
Validation must prevent invalid configuration states (for example missing required fields, invalid email formats, or conflicting rules).
Reset/Cancel actions revert unsaved changes to prevent accidental misconfiguration.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
The table below lists the minimum data elements that are displayed, captured, or affected on this screen. The intent is to provide a design-time data contract that supports implementation, integration planning, and reporting consistency.

Pagination and, where relevant, export controls.
When implemented together, these components provide a consistent and predictable experience across the portal, reduce training needs, and ensure that users can complete the intended workflow with minimal friction.
The key user interactions and system behaviors expected on this screen are listed below. These behaviors cover navigation, validation, permissions, notifications, and audit requirements implied by the wireframe.
Add/edit actions open the corresponding configuration form; save applies changes and updates dependent routing/SLA behavior.
Disable/delete actions must require confirmation and must protect system-critical defaults from accidental removal.
Ordering controls affect how items appear in dropdowns and routing logic, and must be preserved consistently.
Implementing these behaviors consistently ensures that the e-GRM remains reliable, auditable, and secure, while supporting decentralized case handling and clear accountability for actions taken on grievances and tasks.
